class="header center-on-small-only">\n        <a href="https://github.com/kresCruz/angular-materialize" style="color:white;">\n         Angular-materialize\n        </a>\n       </h1>\n       <p class="center-on-small-only" style="color: white;">\n        This is a collection of simple angular directives for using the features in\n        <a href="http://materializecss.com">\n         materializecss\n        </a>\n        .\n       </p>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class="container">\n    <div class="row" id="about">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      About angular-materialize\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This plugin is useful for you if you want to use the\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/">\n       Materialize UI framework\n      </a>\n      with angular.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      It includes a number of directives, which makes sure that the components in materialize.js, which are mainly initialized on document ready, are handled by Angular in the right way.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      So it is not a complete rewrite of Materialize. And it therefore depends on jQuery, because Materialize depends on jQuery.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Below is a small example to get you started, and below that documentation for the directives which are included in this plugin.\n      <br/>\n      Some parts of materialize, like the CSS framework, doesn\'t require anything extra to work in an Angular context, and they are therefore not covered here.\n      <br/>\n      A list of the features in Materialize which does not yet work with angular-materialize can be found in\n      <a href="https://github.com/krescruz/angular-materialize/blob/master/README.md#missing-features">\n       the readme on Github\n      </a>\n      .\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="getting-started">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Getting started\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This plugin and all of its dependencies are hosted on CDNs, which makes setup easy.\n      <br/>\n id="input-field">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Input-field\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Materialize uses the class .input-field to manage animating labels and input-fields. But that doesn\'t work properly when angular dynamically creates element\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Instead of adding the class input-field, use the input-field directive. This way it still works when angular dynamically creates it.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Just in Materialize, if you add the length attribute, a character-counter will appear (in the below length is set to 150).\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       input\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       textarea\n      </code>\n      tags has to be direct children of the element with the input-field tag.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" ng-init="showInputLabel = true;dummyInputs.inputFieldInput = \'This is input\'; dummyInputs.textAreaInput = \'Textareas \\ncan\\ncontain\\nmultiple\\nlines\';">\n     <div class="col s2">\n      <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showInputLabel = !showInputLabel">\n       Toggle input\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <div class="col s4 ng-scope" ng-if="showInputLabel">\n      <div class="ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n       <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n        <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="angularMaterializeID1" length="150" ng-model="dummyInputs.inputFieldInput" type="text"/>\n        <label class="ng-scope active" for="angularMaterializeID1">\n         Input label\n        </label>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <!-- end ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <!-- ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <div class="col s3 ng-scope" ng-if="showInputLabel">\n      <div class="ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n       <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n        <textarea class="materialize-textarea ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="angularMaterializeID2" ng-model="dummyInputs.textAreaInput" style="height: 104.991px;"></textarea>\n        <label class="ng-scope active" for="angularMaterializeID2">\n         Textarea\n id="input-clock">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Input-clock\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This is a wrapper made around the\n      <a href="https://github.com/chingyawhao/materialize-clockpicker">\n       materialize-clockpicker made by chingyawhao\n      </a>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The bundled JavaScript only includes the wrapper JavaScript, and for this to work you need to include the JavaScript and CSS from\n      <a href="https://github.com/chingyawhao/materialize-clockpicker">\n       materialize-clockpicker\n      </a>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The options for this wrapper are the same as the options for the original materialize-clockpicker.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Below is a small example, where the option\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       twelvehour\n      </code>\n      has been set to false.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <label for="input_starttime">\n      Time\n     </label>\n     <input class="ng-isolate-scope timepicker" data-twelvehour="false" id="input_starttime" input-clock="" type="text"/>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="select">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Material select\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Add the material-select as an attribute to the select where you want material-select.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Not needed if you add the class browser-default.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      It doesn\'t support changing content within the select, add the class browser-default if you want that.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       watch\n      </code>\n      , then the material-select will re-initialize whenever something changes in the content within the select.\n      <br/>\n      That includes if the number of list elements change.\n      <br/>\n      But beware, while the implementation works, it is very heavy in computation, so tread lightly.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <div class="section col s4">\n HTML5 range element without needing to use a directive or extra JavaScript.\n              If you want to use the noUiSlider jQuery plugin that ships with materializecss,\n              you\'ll need to include\n      <a href="https://cdnjs.com/libraries/noUiSlider">\n       noUiSlider\'s JS and CSS file\n      </a>\n      and use the\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       nouislider\n      </code>\n      directive.\n      <br/>\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">div</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/nouislider" target="_blank">nouislider</a> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/ng-model" target="_blank">ng-model</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>value<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/min" target="_blank">min</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>5<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/max" target="_blank">max</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>300<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;/</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">div</a></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span><span class="token lf">\n</span></code></pre>\n     <p>\n      See\n      <a href="http://refreshless.com/nouislider/slider-options/">\n       noUiSlider\'s docs\n      </a>\n      for how to use it. Supported config options are: ngModel (required), min, max, step, connect, and tooltips.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="carousel">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Carousel\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      A simple directive, that enables the carousel. Just add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       carousel\n      </code>\n      , and the carousel will be initialized.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can optionally set one of more of the attributes\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       duration\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       dist\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       shift\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       padding\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       full-width\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       height\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       indicators\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       no-wrap\n      </code>\n      , and the option will be passed to the slider.\n      <br/>\n      Like so:\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/carousel" target="_blank">\n         carousel\n        </a>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/duration" target="_blank">\n         duration\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'500\'\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/no-wrap" target="_blank">\n         no-wrap\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'true\'\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;/\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </code>\n      <br/>\n      The options correspond to the options in the\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/carousel.html">\n       Materialize documentation\n      </a>\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <div carousel="" class="ng-isolate-scope carousel initialized">\n      <a class="carousel-item active" href="javascript:void(0);" style="z-index: 0; opacity: 1; display: block; transform: translateX(255px) translateY(100px) translateX(0px) translateX(0px) translateZ(0px);">\n       <img src="images/nature1.jpg"/>\n      </a>\n      <a class="carousel-item" href="javascript:void(0);" style="transform: translateX(255px) translateY(100px) populated using ng-repeat, just to show that it is possible. You can also just manually put in the content.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      In the below, the popout class is added, which makes a "Google inbox" effect. Just remove the popout class to get a normal accordion.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Since this is just a wrapper for materializes collapsible,\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/collapsible.html">\n       all their customization\n      </a>\n      can be used.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       watch\n      </code>\n      , then the collapsible will re-initialize whenever something changes in the content within the collapsible.\n      <br/>\n      That includes if the number of list elements change.\n      <br/>\n      But beware, while the implementation works, it is very heavy in computation, so tread lightly.\n     </p>\n     <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showCollapsible = !showCollapsible" ng-init="showCollapsible = true">\n      Show/hide the below collapsible\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <!-- ngIf: showCollapsible -->\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="CollapsibleController" ng-if="showCollapsible">\n     <ul class="collapsible popout" data-collapsible="accordion" watch="">\n      <!-- ngRepeat: single in collapsibleElements -->\n      <li class="ng-scope" ng-repeat="single in collapsibleElements">\n       <div class="collapsible-header ng-binding">\n        <i class="mdi-image-filter-drama">\n        </i>\n        First\n       </div>\n       <div class="collapsible-body">\n        <p class="ng-binding">\n         Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet.\n        </p>\n       </div>\n      </li>\n      <!-- end ngRepeat: single in collapsibleElements -->\n      <li class="ng-scope" ng-repeat="single in collapsibleElements">\n       <div class="collapsible-header ng-binding">\n        <i class="mdi-maps-place">\n        </i>\n        Second\n       </div>\n       <div class="collapsible-body">\n        <p class="ng-binding">\n         Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet.\n        </p>\n       </div>\n      </li>\n      <!-- end ngRepeat: single in collapsibleElements -->\n      <li class="ng-scope" ng-repeat="single in collapsibleElements">\n       <div class="collapsible-header ng-binding">\n        <i class="mdi-social-whatshot">\n        </i>\n        Third\n       </div>\n       <div class="collapsible-body">\n        <p class="ng-binding">\n         Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet.\n        </p>\n       </div>\n      </li>\n      <!-- end ngRepeat: single in collapsibleElements -->\n     </ul>\n    </div>\n    <!-- end ngIf: showCollapsible -->\n  The chips attribute makes sure the jQuery Plugin is run. Use this directive if you want a dynamic chips functionality.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       secondary-placeholder\n      </code>\n      is the text you see when there is no item.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      And\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       placeholder\n      </code>\n      is the text you see when there is more than one item.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="ChipsController">\n     <div>\n      <div chips="" class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-isolate-scope ng-not-empty chips" data-index="0" data-initialized="true" ng-model="chips" placeholder="Add another" secondary-placeholder="Add">\n       <div class="chip">\n        Apple\n        <i class="material-icons close">\n         close\n        </i>\n       </div>\n       <div class="chip">\n        Microsoft\n        <i class="material-icons close">\n         close\n class="header">\n      Toasts\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Materializes toast is a global function. Using this directive you can call a toast using a custom event (in the below click), and show a message determined by a variable in the scope.\n      <br/>\n      The message is specified through the message attribute, and the duration is set though the duration attribute (defaults to 3000ms if not set).\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="ToastController">\n     <div class="col s4 ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n      <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="message" ng-init="dummyInputs.message = \'I\\\'m a message\'" ng-model="dummyInputs.message" type="text"/>\n       <label class="ng-scope active" for="message">\n        Message\n       </label>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <div class="col s2 ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n      <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="toastDuration" ng-init="dummyInputs.duration = 1000" ng-model="dummyInputs.duration" type="text"/>\n       <label class="ng-scope active" for="toastDuration">\n        Toast duration\n       </label>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <div class="input-field col s4">\n      <a callback="callback(\'Your toast was dismissed\')" class="waves-effect waves-light btn ng-isolate-scope" duration="1000" message="I\'m a message" toast="click">\n       Toast!\n      </a>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" id="pushpin">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Pushpin\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin\n      </code>\n      attribute allows you to pin a particular element to the top of the page.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can use the\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-top\n      </code>\n      attribute to define distance in pixels from the top of the page where the element becomes fixed. The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-offset\n      </code>\n      attribute can be used to offset the distance from the top. The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-bottom\n      </code>\n      attribute can be used to set the distance in pixels from the top of the page where the elements stops being fixed.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" ng-controller="ModalController" ng-init="dummyInputs.modalInput = \'Modal header\'">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Modals\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      You need a modal trigger, like the below. The trigger should have the modal directive, and the href attribute must point to the ID of the modal structure.\n      <br/>\n      The modal strcture should be structured\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/modals.html">\n       just like in materialize\n      </a>\n      .\n      <br/>\n      In the below example, you can change the header of the modal through the input field.\n     </p>\n     <!-- Modal Trigger -->\n     <div class="col">\n      <a class="btn ng-isolate-scope" complete="completeCallback()" data-target="demoModal" modal="" open="openModal" ready="readyCallback()">\n       <span class="ng-scope">\n        Show Modal\n       </span>\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <div class="col s4 ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n      <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="angularMaterializeID0" ng-model="dummyInputs.modalInput" type="text"/>\n       <label class="ng-scope active" for="angularMaterializeID0">\n        Modal header\n       </label>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <div class="col s4">\n      <a class="btn" ng-click="openModal = true">\n       Open from controller\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- Modal Structure -->\n     <div class="modal" id="demoModal" style="top: 4%; opacity: 0; transform: scaleX(0.7); display: none;">\n      <div class="modal-content">\n       <h4 class="ng-binding">\n        Modal header\n       </h4>\n       <p>\n        A bunch of text\n       </p>\n      </div>\n      <div ng-init="showParallax = true">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Parallax\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Adding the parallax attribute makes sure that\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/parallax.html">\n       the jQuery plugin from Materialize\n      </a>\n      is run.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      It works just like the code below the image shows, and fills the entire width of the container it is put in.\n     </p>\n     <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showParallax = !showParallax">\n      Show/hide the below parallax\n     </a>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <!-- ngIf: showParallax -->\n   <div class="parallax-container ng-scope" ng-if="showParallax" style="margin: 20px 0;">\n    <div class="parallax" parallax="">\n     <img src="images/parallax1.jpg" style="display: block;"/>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <!-- end ngIf: showParallax -->\n   <div class="container">\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token id="scrollfire">\n     <h2 class="header ng-isolate-scope" offset="500" scroll-fire="toast(\'Past scoll-fire\', 2000)">\n      ScrollFire\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      It\'s previously stated that this library is mostly wrappers for Materialize code.\n      <br/>\n      This directive is an exception, since the Materialize code for ScrollFire is crap (as of version 0.97.5).\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      ScrollFire is very simple, you set an attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       scoll-fire\n      </code>\n      on some attribute, with a callback. And this callback fires when the user scrolls past that element.\n      <br/>\n      One can further set an\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       offset\n      </code>\n      attribute, to make the callback fire after the user has scrolled a certain amount of pixels beyond the element.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you look at the source of this directive, it is used to alert a message after the user has scrolled 500 pixels past the "ScrollFire" header.\n      <br/>\n      And the code below shows the source-code for that header. That example requires an\n      <code class=" language-javascript" data-language="javascript">\n       toast\n      </code>\n      function to be defined on the scope.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/h2" target="_blank">h2</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/class" target="_blank">class</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>header<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/scroll-fire" target="_blank">scroll-fire</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>toast(\'Past scoll-fire\', 2000)<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/offset" target="_blank">offset</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>500<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span>ScrollFire<span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;/</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/h2" target="_blank">h2</a></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="sidenav">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Sidenav\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Make sure to have a side-menu with id corresponding to the argument\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       data-activates\n      </code>\n      .\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you copy this page, there is another side-nav link in the top of the page, which initializes first and therefore sets the options.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the class\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       button-collapse\n      </code>\n      the button will only show when the side-menu is hidden.\n      <br/>\n      This is not done on the below button, for demonstration purposes, although it is added in the code example.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <a class="top-nav btn waves-effect waves-light ng-isolate-scope" data-activates="nav-mobile" data-closeonclick="false" data-sidenav="left" href="#">\n      Show side-nav\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/a" target="_blank">a</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/href" punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>nav-mobile<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <span class="token attr-name">data-sidenav</span><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>left<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <span class="token attr-name">data-menuwidth</span><span punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="slider">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Slider\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      An extremely simple directive, that just enables the slider. Just add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       slider\n      </code>\n      , and the slider will be initialized.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can optionally set one of more of the attributes\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       height\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       transition\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       interval\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       indicators\n      </code>\n      , and the option will be passed to the slider.\n      <br/>\n      Like so:\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/slider" target="_blank">\n         slider\n        </a>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/height" target="_blank">\n         height\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'500\'\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/transition" target="_blank">\n         transition\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'400\'\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;/\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </code>\n      <br/>\n      The options correspond to the ones in the\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/media.html#slider">\n       Materialize documentation\n      </a>\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <div class="ng-isolate-scope slider" slider="" class="caption">\n      Materialbox is intialized automatically. However, if you add images dynamically, you will have to add this initialization code.\n     </p>\n     <div class="material-placeholder">\n      <div class="material-placeholder">\n       <img class="materialboxed responsive-img initialized" materialboxed="" src="images/sample-1.jpg" width="650"/>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <p>\n      Creating the above image with the effect is as simple as adding a  class to the image tag.\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" add a short caption to your photo. Just add the caption as a\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       data-caption\n      </code>\n      attribute.\n     </p>\n     <div class="material-placeholder">\n      <div class="material-placeholder">\n       <img class="materialboxed initialized" data-caption="A picture of some deer and tons of trees" materialboxed="" src="images/nature_portrait_by_pw_fotografie-d63tx0n.jpg" width="250"/>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <p>\n      Creating the above image with the effect is as Tabs\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       This is a very simple directive, that just calls the jQuery plugin when the element is initialized.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For the styling to work, you still need to have the class\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        tabs\n       </code>\n       on the\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        ul\n       </code>\n       tag\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of the simple implementation, don\'t expect ng-repeat ng-model or similar to work inside the ul of the tabs (should work inside the content though).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is possible to trigger reload of tabs manually with a simple boolean property on your scope. It can be useful when you want to load your content dynamically with\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        ng-include\n       </code>\n       or so.\n      </p>\n      <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showTabs = !showTabs">\n       Show/hide the below tabs\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- ngIf: showTabs -->\n     <div class="row ng-scope" punctuation">&lt;/</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">div</a></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;/</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">div</a></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n     </div>\n     <div class="row" id="pagination">\n      <h2 class="header">\n       Pagination\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       This is only the pagination buttons, it doesn\'t do anything to change the page. That you\'ll have to do in the callback\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the below, changePage is a function defined on the controller.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Pr. default the prev/next buttons are icons from\n       <a href="http://google.github.io/material-design-icons/">\n        Material design icons\n       </a>\n       , which needs to be included, like this:\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token tag">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           &lt;\n          </span>\n          <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/link" target="_blank">\n           link\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/href" target="_blank">\n          href\n         </a>\n         <span class="token attr-value">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n          <a class="token url-link" href="https://fonts.googleapis.com/icon">\n           https://fonts.googleapis.com/icon\n          </a>\n          ?family\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          Material+Icons\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/rel" target="_blank">\n          rel\n         </a>\n         <span class="token attr-value">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n          stylesheet\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &gt;\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </code>\n       <br/>\n       It is also possible to set the option\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        use-simple-prev-next\n       </code>\n       to false, in which case simple "&gt;" chars will be used.\n      </p>\n     </div>\n     <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="PaginationController">\n      <pagination class="header center-on-small-only">\n        <a href="https://github.com/kresCruz/angular-materialize" style="color:white;">\n         Angular-materialize\n        </a>\n       </h1>\n       <p class="center-on-small-only" style="color: white;">\n        This is a collection of simple angular directives for using the features in\n        <a href="http://materializecss.com">\n         materializecss\n        </a>\n        .\n       </p>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class="container">\n    <div class="row" id="about">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      About angular-materialize\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This plugin is useful for you if you want to use the\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/">\n       Materialize UI framework\n      </a>\n      with angular.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      It includes a number of directives, which makes sure that the components in materialize.js, which are mainly initialized on document ready, are handled by Angular in the right way.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      So it is not a complete rewrite of Materialize. And it therefore depends on jQuery, because Materialize depends on jQuery.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Below is a small example to get you started, and below that documentation for the directives which are included in this plugin.\n      <br/>\n      Some parts of materialize, like the CSS framework, doesn\'t require anything extra to work in an Angular context, and they are therefore not covered here.\n      <br/>\n      A list of the features in Materialize which does not yet work with angular-materialize can be found in\n      <a href="https://github.com/krescruz/angular-materialize/blob/master/README.md#missing-features">\n       the readme on Github\n      </a>\n      .\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="getting-started">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Getting started\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This plugin and all of its dependencies are hosted on CDNs, which makes setup easy.\n      <br/>\n      To get a minimal example up and running, copy the below into index.html and app.js:\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" id="input-field">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Input-field\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Materialize uses the class .input-field to manage animating labels and input-fields. But that doesn\'t work properly when angular dynamically creates element\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Instead of adding the class input-field, use the input-field directive. This way it still works when angular dynamically creates it.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Just in Materialize, if you add the length attribute, a character-counter will appear (in the below length is set to 150).\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       input\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       textarea\n      </code>\n      tags has to be direct children of the element with the input-field tag.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" ng-init="showInputLabel = true;dummyInputs.inputFieldInput = \'This is input\'; dummyInputs.textAreaInput = \'Textareas \\ncan\\ncontain\\nmultiple\\nlines\';">\n     <div class="col s2">\n      <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showInputLabel = !showInputLabel">\n       Toggle input\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <div class="col s4 ng-scope" ng-if="showInputLabel">\n      <div class="ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n       <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n        <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="angularMaterializeID1" length="150" ng-model="dummyInputs.inputFieldInput" type="text"/>\n        <label class="ng-scope active" for="angularMaterializeID1">\n         Input label\n        </label>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <!-- end ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <!-- ngIf: showInputLabel -->\n     <div class="col s3 ng-scope" ng-if="showInputLabel">\n class="row" id="input-date">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Input-date\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      The below example is where there are values in all the options, but all the options are optional.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The attributes\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       min\n      </code>\n      and\n      <code class=" language-markup" Date Constructor\n      </a>\n      .\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="DateController">\n     <label class="active" for="inputCreated">\n      Input date\n id="input-clock">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Input-clock\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      This is a wrapper made around the\n      <a href="https://github.com/chingyawhao/materialize-clockpicker">\n       materialize-clockpicker made by chingyawhao\n      </a>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The bundled JavaScript only includes the wrapper JavaScript, and for this to work you need to include the JavaScript and CSS from\n      <a href="https://github.com/chingyawhao/materialize-clockpicker">\n       materialize-clockpicker\n      </a>\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      The options for this wrapper are the same as the options for the original materialize-clockpicker.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Below is a small example, where the option\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       twelvehour\n      </code>\n      has been set to false.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <label for="input_starttime">\n      Time\n     </label>\n     <input class="ng-isolate-scope timepicker" data-twelvehour="false" id="input_starttime" input-clock="" type="text"/>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="select">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Material select\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Add the material-select as an attribute to the select where you want material-select.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Not needed if you add the class browser-default.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      It doesn\'t support changing content within the select, add the class browser-default if you want that.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       watch\n      </code>\n      , then the material-select will re-initialize whenever something changes in the content within the select.\n      <br/>\n      That includes if the number of list elements change.\n      <br/>\n      But beware, while the implementation works, it is very heavy in computation, so tread lightly.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <div class="section col s4">\n HTML5 range element without needing to use a directive or extra JavaScript.\n              If you want to use the noUiSlider jQuery plugin that ships with materializecss,\n              you\'ll need to include\n      <a href="https://cdnjs.com/libraries/noUiSlider">\n       noUiSlider\'s JS and CSS file\n      </a>\n      and use the\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       nouislider\n      </code>\n      directive.\n      <br/>\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">div</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/nouislider" target="_blank">nouislider</a> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/ng-model" target="_blank">ng-model</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token class="token lf">\n</span></code></pre>\n     <p>\n      See\n      <a href="http://refreshless.com/nouislider/slider-options/">\n       noUiSlider\'s docs\n      </a>\n      for how to use it. Supported config options are: ngModel (required), min, max, step, connect, and tooltips.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="carousel">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Carousel\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      A simple directive, that enables the carousel. Just add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       carousel\n      </code>\n      , and the carousel will be initialized.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can optionally set one of more of the attributes\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       duration\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       dist\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       shift\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       padding\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       full-width\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       height\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       indicators\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       no-wrap\n      </code>\n      , and the option will be passed to the slider.\n      <br/>\n      Like so:\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/carousel" target="_blank">\n         carousel\n        </a>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/duration" target="_blank">\n         duration\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'500\'\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/no-wrap" target="_blank">\n         no-wrap\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'true\'\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;/\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </code>\n      <br/>\n      The options correspond to the options in the\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/carousel.html">\n       Materialize documentation\n      </a>\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <div carousel="" class="ng-isolate-scope carousel populated using ng-repeat, just to show that it is possible. You can also just manually put in the content.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      In the below, the popout class is added, which makes a "Google inbox" effect. Just remove the popout class to get a normal accordion.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      Since this is just a wrapper for materializes collapsible,\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/collapsible.html">\n       all their customization\n      </a>\n      can be used.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       watch\n      </code>\n      , then the collapsible will re-initialize whenever something changes in the content within the collapsible.\n      <br/>\n      That includes if the number of list elements change.\n      <br/>\n      But beware, while the implementation works, it is very heavy in computation, so tread lightly.\n     </p>\n     <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showCollapsible = !showCollapsible" ng-init="showCollapsible = true">\n      Show/hide the below collapsible\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <!-- ngIf: showCollapsible -->\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="CollapsibleController" ng-if="showCollapsible">\n     <ul class="collapsible popout" data-collapsible="accordion" watch="">\n      <!-- ngRepeat: single in collapsibleElements -->\n      <li class="ng-scope" ng-repeat="single in collapsibleElements">\n       <div class="collapsible-header ng-binding">\n        <i class="mdi-image-filter-drama">\n        </i>\n        First\n       </div>\n       <div class="collapsible-body">\n        <p class="ng-binding">\n         Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet.\n        </p>\n  The chips attribute makes sure the jQuery Plugin is run. </code>\n      is the text you see when there is no item.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      And\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       placeholder\n      </code>\n      is the class="header">\n      Toasts\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Materializes toast is a global function. Using this directive you can call a toast using a custom event (in the below click), and show a message determined by a variable in the scope.\n      <br/>\n      The message is specified through the message attribute, and the duration is set though the duration attribute (defaults to 3000ms if not set).\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="ToastController">\n attributes on the tag, matching the names of the options in the materializeCSS\'s version.\n                You can disable tooltip, passing false to tooltipped attribute.\n     </p>\n     <div class="col s4">\n      <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showTooltippedButtons = !showTooltippedButtons" ng-init="showTooltippedButtons = true" style="margin-bottom: 10px;">\n id="pushpin">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Pushpin\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin\n      </code>\n      attribute allows you to pin a particular element to the top of the page.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can use the\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-top\n      </code>\n      attribute to define distance in pixels from the top of the page where the element becomes fixed. The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-offset\n      </code>\n      attribute can be used to offset the distance from the top. The\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       pushpin-bottom\n      </code>\n      attribute can be used to set the distance in pixels from the top of the page where the elements stops being fixed.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span ng-controller="ModalController" ng-init="dummyInputs.modalInput = \'Modal header\'">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Modals\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      You need a modal trigger, like the below. The trigger should have the modal directive, and the href attribute must point to the ID of the modal structure.\n      <br/>\n      The modal strcture should be structured\n      <a href="http://materializecss.com/modals.html">\n       just like in materialize\n      </a>\n      .\n      <br/>\n      In the below example, you can change the header of the modal through the input field.\n     </p>\n     <!-- Modal Trigger -->\n     <div class="col">\n      <a class="btn ng-isolate-scope" complete="completeCallback()" data-target="demoModal" modal="" open="openModal" ready="readyCallback()">\n       <span class="ng-scope">\n        Show Modal\n       </span>\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <div class="col s4 ng-isolate-scope" input-field="">\n      <div class="input-field" ng-transclude="">\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-untouched ng-valid ng-scope ng-not-empty" id="angularMaterializeID0" ng-model="dummyInputs.modalInput" type="text"/>\n       <label class="ng-scope active" for="angularMaterializeID0">\n        Modal header\n       </label>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n     <div class="col s4">\n      <a class="btn" ng-click="openModal = true">\n       Open from controller\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- Modal Structure -->\n     <div class="modal" id="demoModal" style="top: 4%; opacity: 0; transform: scaleX(0.7); display: none;">\n      <div class="modal-content">\n       <h4 class="ng-binding">\n        Modal header\n       </h4>\n       <p>\n        A bunch of text\n       </p>\n      </div>\n      <div id="scrollfire">\n     <h2 class="header ng-isolate-scope" offset="500" scroll-fire="toast(\'Past scoll-fire\', 2000)">\n      ScrollFire\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      It\'s previously stated that this library is mostly wrappers for Materialize code.\n      <br/>\n      This directive is an exception, since the Materialize code for ScrollFire is crap (as of version 0.97.5).\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      ScrollFire is very simple, you set an attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       scoll-fire\n      </code>\n      on some attribute, with a callback. And this callback fires when the user scrolls past that element.\n      <br/>\n      One can further set an\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       offset\n      </code>\n      attribute, to make the callback fire after the user has scrolled a certain amount of pixels beyond the element.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you look at the source of this directive, it is used to alert a message after the user has scrolled 500 pixels past the "ScrollFire" header.\n      <br/>\n      And the code below shows the source-code for that header. That example requires an\n      <code class=" language-javascript" data-language="javascript">\n       toast\n      </code>\n      function to be defined on the scope.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/h2" target="_blank">h2</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/class" target="_blank">class</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token target="_blank">scroll-fire</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>toast(\'Past scoll-fire\', 2000)<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/offset" target="_blank">offset</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>500<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span>ScrollFire<span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;/</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/h2" target="_blank">h2</a></span><span class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="sidenav">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Sidenav\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      Make sure to have a side-menu with id corresponding to the argument\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       data-activates\n      </code>\n      .\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you copy this page, there is another side-nav link in the top of the page, which initializes first and therefore sets the options.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      If you add the class\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       button-collapse\n      </code>\n      the button will only show when the side-menu is hidden.\n      <br/>\n      This is not done on the below button, for demonstration purposes, although it is added in the code example.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <a class="top-nav btn waves-effect waves-light ng-isolate-scope" data-activates="nav-mobile" data-closeonclick="false" data-sidenav="left" href="#">\n      Show side-nav\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" punctuation">&gt;</span></span></code></pre>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row" id="slider">\n     <h2 class="header">\n      Slider\n     </h2>\n     <p>\n      An extremely simple directive, that just enables the slider. Just add the attribute\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       slider\n      </code>\n      , and the slider will be initialized.\n     </p>\n     <p>\n      You can optionally set one of more of the attributes\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       height\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       transition\n      </code>\n      ,\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       interval\n      </code>\n      or\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       indicators\n      </code>\n      , and the option will be passed to the slider.\n      <br/>\n      Like so:\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/slider" target="_blank">\n         slider\n        </a>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/height" target="_blank">\n         height\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'500\'\n        </span>\n        <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/transition" target="_blank">\n         transition\n        </a>\n        <span class="token attr-value">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          =\n         </span>\n         \'400\'\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <span class="token tag">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &lt;/\n         </span>\n         <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/div" target="_blank">\n          div\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <span class="token punctuation">\n         &gt;\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </code>\n      <br/>\n      The options correspond to the ones in the\n      <a class="caption">\n      Materialbox is intialized automatically. However, if you add images dynamically, you will have to add this initialization code.\n     </p>\n     <div class="material-placeholder">\n      <div class="material-placeholder">\n       <img class="materialboxed responsive-img initialized" materialboxed="" src="images/sample-1.jpg" width="650"/>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <p>\n      Creating the above image with the effect is as simple as adding a  class to the image tag.\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>materialboxed responsive-img<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" add a short caption to your photo. Just add the caption as a\n      <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n       data-caption\n      </code>\n      attribute.\n     </p>\n     <div class="material-placeholder">\n      <div class="material-placeholder">\n       <img class="materialboxed initialized" data-caption="A picture of some deer and tons of trees" materialboxed="" src="images/nature_portrait_by_pw_fotografie-d63tx0n.jpg" width="250"/>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="row">\n     <p>\n      Creating the above image with the effect is as simple as adding a  class to the image tag.\n     </p>\n     <pre class=" language-markup"><code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup" ng-non-bindable=""><span class="token lf">\n</span><span class="token tag"><span class="token tag"><span class="token punctuation">&lt;</span><a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/img" target="_blank">img</a></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/materialboxed" target="_blank">materialboxed</a> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/class" target="_blank">class</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>materialboxed<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <span class="token attr-name">data-caption</span><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token punctuation">"</span>A picture of some deer and tons of trees<span class="token punctuation">"</span></span> <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/width" target="_blank">width</a><span class="token attr-value"><span class="token punctuation">=</span><span class="token class="token punctuation">&gt;</span></span><span class="token lf">\n</span>            </code></pre>\n     <div class="row" id="tabs" ng-init="showTabs = true">\n      <h2 class="header">\n       Tabs\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       This is a very simple directive, that just calls the jQuery plugin when the element is initialized.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For the styling to work, you still need to have the class\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        tabs\n       </code>\n       on the\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        ul\n       </code>\n       tag\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of the simple implementation, don\'t expect ng-repeat ng-model or similar to work inside the ul of the tabs (should work inside the content though).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is possible to trigger reload of tabs manually with a simple boolean property on your scope. It can be useful when you want to load your content dynamically with\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        ng-include\n       </code>\n       or so.\n      </p>\n      <a class="btn waves-effect waves-light" ng-click="showTabs = !showTabs">\n       Show/hide the below tabs\n      </a>\n     </div>\n     <!-- ngIf: showTabs -->\n     <div class="row ng-scope" </h2>\n      <p>\n       This is only the pagination buttons, it doesn\'t do anything to change the page. That you\'ll have to do in the callback\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the below, changePage is a function defined on the controller.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Pr. default the prev/next buttons are icons from\n       <a href="http://google.github.io/material-design-icons/">\n        Material design icons\n       </a>\n       , which needs to be included, like this:\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        <span class="token tag">\n         <span class="token tag">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           &lt;\n          </span>\n          <a class="token tag-id" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/elements/link" target="_blank">\n           link\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/href" target="_blank">\n          href\n         </a>\n         <span class="token attr-value">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n          <a class="token url-link" href="https://fonts.googleapis.com/icon">\n           https://fonts.googleapis.com/icon\n          </a>\n          ?family\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          Material+Icons\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <a class="token attr-name" href="http://docs.webplatform.org/wiki/html/attributes/rel" target="_blank">\n          rel\n         </a>\n         <span class="token attr-value">\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           =\n          </span>\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n          stylesheet\n          <span class="token punctuation">\n           "\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="token punctuation">\n          &gt;\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </code>\n       <br/>\n       It is also possible to set the option\n       <code class=" language-markup" data-language="markup">\n        use-simple-prev-next\n       </code>\n       to false, in which case simple "&gt;" chars will be used.\n      </p>\n     </div>\n     <div class="row ng-scope" ng-controller="PaginationController">\n      <pagination
